I found the issue. Looking at the `read_cache()` method on lines 204-230, I can see the problem:\n\n```python\ndef read_cache(self) -> None:\n    \"\"\"Initialize the adblocking engine from cache file.\"\"\"\n    try:\n        cache_exists = self._cache_path.is_file()\n    except OSError:\n        logger.error(\"Failed to read adblock cache\", exc_info=True)\n        return\n\n    if cache_exists:\n        logger.debug(\"Loading cached adblock data: %s\", self._cache_path)\n        try:\n            self._engine.deserialize_from_file(str(self._cache_path))\n        except ValueError as e:\n            if str(e) != \"DeserializationError\":\n                # All Rust exceptions get turned into a ValueError by\n                # python-adblock\n                raise\n            message.error(\"Reading adblock filter data failed (corrupted data?). \"\n                          \"Please run :adblock-update.\")\n    else:\n        if (\n            config.val.content.blocking.adblock.lists\n            and not self._has_basedir\n            and config.val.content.blocking.enabled\n            and self.enabled\n        ):\n            message.info(\"Run :adblock-update to get adblock lists.\")\n```\n\nThe bug is in the exception handling:\n- Lines 215-220: When `deserialize_from_file()` raises a `ValueError`, the code checks if the string representation equals `\"DeserializationError\"`.\n- If it doesn't match exactly, it re-raises the exception (line 220: `raise`)\n- However, if the corrupted cache causes a different ValueError message, the exception will be re-raised and crash the application.\n- The intent seems to be to catch the specific \"DeserializationError\" and handle it gracefully, but the logic is wrong - if the error message is NOT \"DeserializationError\", it raises, which is backwards!\n\n\n- Actually, re-reading the comment on lines 217-219, it states that all Rust exceptions become ValueError objects through python-adblock, so deserialization failures should produce a ValueError with message \"DeserializationError\". The logic then makes sense: if the message matches the expected error, handle it gracefully; if it's a different ValueError, re-raise since it's unexpected. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01JF3P4qKGL1ZyUUFDAUy8zS","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I see the existing tests. I notice there's a `test_adblock_cache` test but it doesn't test the case of a corrupted cache file. Let me look more carefully at the `read_cache()` method again to understand the bug.\n\nLooking at lines 204-230 of braveadblock.py:\n\n```python\ndef read_cache(self) -> None:\n    \"\"\"Initialize the adblocking engine from cache file.\"\"\"\n    try:\n        cache_exists = self._cache_path.is_file()\n    except OSError:\n        logger.error(\"Failed to read adblock cache\", exc_info=True)\n        return\n\n    if cache_exists:\n        logger.debug(\"Loading cached adblock data: %s\", self._cache_path)\n        try:\n            self._engine.deserialize_from_file(str(self._cache_path))\n        except ValueError as e:\n            if str(e) != \"DeserializationError\":\n                # All Rust exceptions get turned into a ValueError by\n                # python-adblock\n                raise\n            message.error(\"Reading adblock filter data failed (corrupted data?). \"\n                          \"Please run :adblock-update.\")\n```\n\nThe logic here is:\n1. If a `ValueError` is raised with message \"DeserializationError\", handle it gracefully with `message.error()`\n2. If the message is NOT \"DeserializationError\", re-raise it\n\nBut wait, this seems backwards! The `deserialize_from_file()` method from the `adblock` library raises `adblock.DeserializationError`\n2. The current code only catches `ValueError`, not `adblock.DeserializationError`\n3. Catch deserialization errors gracefully\n2. Log an error message informing the user\n3. Continue running normally (user can browse without ad-blocking until cache is rebuilt)\n\n## Test Contents\n\nThe regression test file contains three test cases:\n\n### 1. `test_corrupted_adblock_cache_does_not_crash` (FAILS - Demonstrates Bug)\n- Creates a corrupted cache file with random bytes\n- Calls `blocker.read_cache()`\n- **Expected:** Should not raise an exception, should call `message.error()`\n- **Actual:** Raises `adblock.DeserializationError` (unhandled)\n\n### 2. `test_corrupted_adblock_cache_message_content` (FAILS - Demonstrates Bug)\n- Creates a corrupted cache file\n- Calls `blocker.read_cache()`\n- **Expected:** Should call `message.error()` with text about cache corruption and `:adblock-update`\n- **Actual:** Exception is raised before `message.error()` can be called\n\n### 3. `test_valid_cache_still_works` (PASSES - Sanity Check)\n- Creates a valid cache file using the `adblock` library\n- Calls `blocker.read_cache()`\n- **Expected:** Should succeed without calling `message.error()`\n- **Actual:** Works correctly (this verifies normal operation is not affected)\n\n## Running the Test\n\n```bash\n# Run all three tests\npython3 -m pytest -c /dev/null --timeout=60 /workspace/regression_test.py\n\n# Run a specific test\npython3 -m pytest -c /dev/null --timeout=60 /workspace/regression_test.py::test_corrupted_adblock_cache_does_not_crash\n\n# With verbose output\npython3 -m pytest -c /dev/null --timeout=60 /workspace/regression_test.py -v\n```\n\n## Test Output\n\nExpected output when running the regression test:\n```\ntest_corrupted_adblock_cache_does_not_crash FAILED     [ 33%]\ntest_corrupted_adblock_cache_message_content FAILED     [ 66%]\ntest_valid_cache_still_works PASSED                    [100%]\n\n2 failed, 1 passed\n```\n\nThe two failures demonstrate the bug exists in the current code. The one passing test confirms that normal cache loading (without corruption) still works.\n\n## Root Cause Analysis\n\nThe bug is in `braveadblock.py` line 214-220:\n\n```python\ntry:\n    self._engine.deserialize_from_file(str(self._cache_path))\nexcept ValueError as e:\n    if str(e) != \"DeserializationError\":\n        raise\n    message.error(\"Reading adblock filter data failed (corrupted data?). \"\n                  \"Please run :adblock-update.\")\n```\n\nThe code catches `ValueError`, but the `adblock` library raises `adblock.DeserializationError` (which is not a `ValueError`). This exception type mismatch causes the error to propagate unhandled.\n\n## Impact\n\nThis bug affects any user whose ad-blocker cache gets corrupted due to:\n- System crash during cache write\n- Disk errors\n- File corruption from other applications\n- Any other cause of cache file corruption\n\nWhen this happens, qutebrowser becomes completely unusable until the user manually finds and deletes the cache file at:\n- Linux: `~/.local/share/qutebrowser/adblock-cache.dat`\n- macOS: `~/Library/Application Support/qutebrowser/adblock-cache.dat`\n- Windows: `%APPDATA%\\qutebrowser\\adblock-cache.dat`\n\n## Fix Strategy (Not Implemented - Test Only)\n\nThe fix would involve catching `adblock.DeserializationError` in addition to `ValueError`:\n\n```python\nexcept (ValueError, adblock.DeserializationError) as e:\n    # Handle the error gracefully\n    message.error(\"Reading adblock filter data failed (corrupted data?). \"\n                  \"Please run :adblock-update.\")\n```\n\nOr checking the exception type more carefully to handle all deserialization errors.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":2,"cache_creation_input_tokens":639,"cache_read_input_tokens":80118,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":639},"output_tokens":2,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"673d7826-4df1-49a3-9652-01a8198efb2d","uuid":"f4ff2f97-c93a-49ba-ada5-6076cb391bfc"}
